        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <p>
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASTP-patch.png">
           <img alt="ASTP-patch.png" data-file-height="5333" data-file-width="5333" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/ASTP-patch.png/180px-ASTP-patch.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/ASTP-patch.png/270px-ASTP-patch.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/ASTP-patch.png/360px-ASTP-patch.png 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
          <br/>
          Official emblem of the Apollo-Soyuz Test Project (ASTP) chosen by NASA and the Soviet Academy of Sciences
          <br/>
         </p>
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg">
          <img alt="Portrait of ASTP crews - restoration.jpg" data-file-height="6586" data-file-width="8232" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg/220px-Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg/330px-Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg/440px-Portrait_of_ASTP_crews_-_restoration.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">
          <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_programme" title="Soyuz programme">
           Soyuz programme
          </a>
         </div>
         <div style="width:100%">
          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">
           ←
           <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_18" title="Soyuz 18">
            Soyuz 18
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">
           <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_20" title="Soyuz 20">
            Soyuz 20
           </a>
           →
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Apollo–Soyuz Test Project
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        ASTP
       </b>
       ) (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru" xml:lang="ru">
        Экспериментальный полёт «Аполлон» - «Союз» (ЭПАС)
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        Eksperimentalniy polyot Apollon-Soyuz
       </i>
       , lit. "Experimental flight Apollo-Soyuz", commonly referred to by the Soviets as "
       <b>
        Soyuz-Apollo
       </b>
       "), conducted in July 1975, was the first joint U.S.–
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        space flight
       </a>
       , as a symbol of the policy of
       <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">
        détente
       </a>
       that the two superpowers were pursuing at the time. It involved the docking of an
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
        Apollo Command/Service Module
       </a>
       with the Soviet
       <a href="#Soyuz_crew">
        Soyuz 19
       </a>
       . The unnumbered Apollo vehicle was a surplus from the terminated
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       and the last one to fly. This mission ceremoniously marked the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">
        Space Race
       </a>
       that had begun in 1957 with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik" title="Sputnik">
        Sputnik
       </a>
       launch.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The mission included both joint and separate scientific experiments (including an engineered
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        eclipse of the Sun
       </a>
       by Apollo to allow Soyuz to take photographs of the solar
       <a href="/wiki/Corona" title="Corona">
        corona
       </a>
       ), and provided useful engineering experience for future joint US–Russian space flights, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle%E2%80%93Mir_Program" title="Shuttle–Mir Program">
        Shuttle–Mir Program
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
        International Space Station
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       ASTP was the last manned US space mission until the first
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttle
       </a>
       flight in April 1981. It was also U.S. astronaut
       <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">
        Donald "Deke" Slayton
       </a>
       's only space flight. He was chosen as one of the original
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">
        Mercury Seven
       </a>
       astronauts in April 1959, but had been grounded until 1972 for medical reasons.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_background">
        Historical background
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Historical background">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2297" data-file-width="2822" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg/220px-Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg/330px-Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg/440px-Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nixon_Kosygin_May_1972.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         U.S. President Richard Nixon and
         <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Premier of the Soviet Union">
          Soviet Premier
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Kosygin" title="Alexei Kosygin">
          Alexei Kosygin
         </a>
         (seated) sign an agreement paving the way for the Apollo–Soyuz flight, May 1972.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The purpose and catalyst of the Apollo–Soyuz Test Project was the policy of
       <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">
        détente
       </a>
       between the two
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
        Cold War
       </a>
       superpowers, the United States and the Soviet Union. Prior to this mission, tensions remained high between the two world superpowers while the United States was engaged in the
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
        Vietnam War
       </a>
       . Meanwhile, the Soviet press was highly critical of the Apollo space missions, printing "the armed intrusion of the United States and Saigon puppets into Laos is a shameless trampling underfoot of international law" over a photograph of the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
        Apollo 14
       </a>
       launch in 1971.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although Soviet leader
       <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">
        Nikita Khrushchev
       </a>
       made the Soviet Union’s policy of détente official in his 1956 doctrine of peaceful coexistence at the
       <a href="/wiki/20th_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">
        20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union
       </a>
       , the two nations seemed to be in perpetual conflict.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to tense relations, space cooperation between the United States and the Soviet Union was unlikely in the early 1970s. On June 7, 1971, the USSR had launched the first piloted orbital space station,
       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">
        Salyut 1
       </a>
       . Meanwhile, the United States had launched the Apollo 14 mission several months prior, the third spacecraft to land humans on the moon. Each side gave the other little coverage whatsoever of their achievements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Both sides had severe criticisms of the other side’s engineering. Soviet spacecraft were designed with automation in mind; the
       <a href="/wiki/Lunokhod_1" title="Lunokhod 1">
        Lunokhod 1
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Luna_16" title="Luna 16">
        Luna 16
       </a>
       were both unmanned probes, and each
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(spacecraft)" title="Soyuz (spacecraft)">
        Soyuz spacecraft
       </a>
       had been designed to minimize risk due to human error by having fewer manual controls with which human operators would have to contend during flight. By contrast, the Apollo spacecraft was designed to be operated by humans and required highly trained astronauts in order to operate. The Soviet Union criticised the Apollo spacecraft as being "extremely complex and dangerous".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Americans also had their own concerns about Soviet spacecraft.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft" title="Christopher C. Kraft">
        Christopher C. Kraft
       </a>
       , director of the
       <a href="/wiki/Johnson_Space_Center" title="Johnson Space Center">
        Manned Spacecraft Center
       </a>
       , criticized the design of the Soyuz: "We in
       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">
        NASA
       </a>
       rely on redundant components--if an instrument fails during flight, our crews switch to another in an attempt to continue the mission. Each Soyuz component, however, is designed for a specific function; if one fails, the cosmonauts land as soon as possible. The Apollo vehicle also relied on astronaut piloting to a much greater extent than did the Soyuz machine".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       American and Soviet engineers already settled their differences for a possible docking of American and Soviet spacecraft in meetings between June and December 1971 in Houston and Moscow, including
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bill_Creasy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bill Creasy (page does not exist)">
        Bill Creasy
       </a>
       ’s design of the
       <a href="/wiki/Androgynous_Peripheral_Attach_System" title="Androgynous Peripheral Attach System">
        Androgynous Peripheral Attach System
       </a>
       between the two ships that would allow either to be active or passive during docking.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battaglia_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Battaglia-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the close of the Vietnam War, relations between the United States and the USSR began to improve, as did the prognosis for a potential cooperative space mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Apollo-Soyuz Test Project was made possible by the thaw in these relations, and the project itself endeavored to amplify and solidify the improving relations between the United States and the Soviet Union. According to Soviet leader
       <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">
        Leonid Brezhnev
       </a>
       , "The Soviet and American spacemen will go up into outer space for the first major joint scientific experiment in the history of mankind. They know that from outer space our planet looks even more beautiful. It is big enough for us to live peacefully on it, but it is too small to be threatened by nuclear war".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thus, both sides recognized ASTP as a political act of peace.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battaglia_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Battaglia-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 1970,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Soviet Academy of Sciences">
        Soviet Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       president
       <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Keldysh" title="Mstislav Keldysh">
        Mstislav Keldysh
       </a>
       responded to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Administrator" title="NASA Administrator">
        NASA Administrator
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_O._Paine" title="Thomas O. Paine">
        Thomas O. Paine
       </a>
       ’s letter proposing a cooperative space mission, and there was subsequently a meeting to discuss technical details. By January 12, U.S. President
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
        Richard Nixon
       </a>
       's Foreign Policy Adviser
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">
        Henry Kissinger
       </a>
       enthusiastically espoused plans for the mission, and expressed these views to NASA administrator George M. Low: "As long as you stick to space, do anything you want to do. You are free to commit--in fact, I want you to tell your counterparts in Moscow that the President has sent you on this mission."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By April 1972, both the United States and the USSR signed an
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Agreement_Concerning_Cooperation_in_the_Exploration_and_Use_of_Outer_Space_for_Peaceful_Purposes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Agreement Concerning Cooperation in the Exploration and Use of Outer Space for Peaceful Purposes (page does not exist)">
        Agreement Concerning Cooperation in the Exploration and Use of Outer Space for Peaceful Purposes
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jennifer_Ross-Nazzal_2010,_pp._29_–_34_6-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jennifer_Ross-Nazzal_2010,_pp._29_–_34-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       committing both the USSR and the United States to the launch of the Apollo–Soyuz Test Project in 1975.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       ASTP was particularly significant for the USSR’s policy of keeping the details of their space program secret from the Soviet people and the world at large, especially Americans. The ASTP was the first Soviet space mission to be televised in a live fashion during the launch, while in space, and during the landing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Soyuz 19 was also the first Soviet spacecraft to which a foreign flight crew had access before flight; the Apollo crew were permitted to inspect it and the launch and crew training site, which was an unprecedented sharing of information with Americans about any Soviet space program.
      </p>
      <p>
       Not all reactions to ASTP were positive. Many Americans feared that ASTP was giving the USSR too much credit in their space program, putting them on equal footing with the sophisticated space exploration efforts of NASA. More feared that the apparent peaceful cooperation between the USSR and the United States would lull people into believing there was no conflict at all between the two superpowers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Soliciting appropriations from the American Congress proved to be quite difficult, which was not a problem in the Soviet Union, and the dedication to space exploration demonstrated by the Soviet Union rejected these criticisms. Some Soviet publicists called American critics of the mission "demagogues who stand against scientific cooperation with the U.S.S.R."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Space_Sciences_1976_2-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-Space_Sciences_1976-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In general, tensions between the United States and the USSR had softened, and the project set a precedent for future cooperative projects in space.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jennifer_Ross-Nazzal_2010,_pp._29_–_34_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Jennifer_Ross-Nazzal_2010,_pp._29_–_34-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Crew_notes">
        Crew notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Crew notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Swigert" title="Jack Swigert">
        Jack Swigert
       </a>
       had originally been assigned as the command module pilot for the ASTP prime crew, but prior to the official announcement he was removed as punishment for his involvement in the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15_postage_stamp_incident" title="Apollo 15 postage stamp incident">
        Apollo 15 postage stamp incident
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Support crew
       </dt>
       <dd>
        <a href="/wiki/Karol_J._Bobko" title="Karol J. Bobko">
         Karol J. Bobko
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Robert_Crippen" title="Robert Crippen">
         Robert Crippen
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Overmyer" title="Robert F. Overmyer">
         Robert F. Overmyer
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Richard_H._Truly" title="Richard H. Truly">
         Richard H. Truly
        </a>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Flight directors
       </dt>
       <dd>
        Pete Frank (Orange team), Neil Hutchinson (Silver team),
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Puddy" title="Don Puddy">
         Don Puddy
        </a>
        (Crimson team), Frank Littleton (Amber team)
       </dd>
      </dl>

       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4164" data-file-width="4084" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg/220px-Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg/330px-Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg/440px-Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Soyuz_Spacecraft_in_Orbit_-_GPN-2002-000155.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Soyuz as seen from Apollo CM
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Apollo–Soyuz Test Project entailed the docking of an American
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
        Apollo Command/Service Module
       </a>
       (CSM) with a Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_7K-TM" title="Soyuz 7K-TM">
        Soyuz 7K-TM
       </a>
       spacecraft. Although the Soyuz was given a mission designation number (Soyuz 19) as part of the ongoing
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_programme" title="Soyuz programme">
        Soyuz program
       </a>
       , its radio call sign was simply "Soyuz" for the duration of the joint mission. The Apollo mission was not a numbered mission of the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">
        Apollo program
       </a>
       , and similarly bore the call sign "Apollo". Despite this, some of the press and a few NASA web pages have referred to the mission as "Apollo 18", but this should not be confused with the
       <a href="/wiki/Canceled_Apollo_missions#Follow-on_lunar_missions" title="Canceled Apollo missions">
        canceled lunar mission
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Apollo spacecraft was launched with a docking module specially designed to enable the two spacecraft to dock with each other, used only once for this mission. The
       <a href="/wiki/Saturn_IB" title="Saturn IB">
        Saturn IB
       </a>
       launch vehicle and CSM were surplus material. Like the
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
        Apollo Lunar Module
       </a>
       , the docking module
       <a href="/wiki/Transposition,_docking,_and_extraction" title="Transposition, docking, and extraction">
        had to be retrieved
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/S-IVB" title="S-IVB">
        S-IVB
       </a>
       upper-stage of the Saturn rocket after launch. The docking module was designed as both an airlock — as the Apollo was pressurized at about 5 psi (340 mbar) using pure oxygen, while the Soyuz used a nitrogen/oxygen atmosphere at
       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure#Mean_sea_level_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">
        sea level pressure
       </a>
       (about 15 psi / 1000 mbar) — and an adapter, since the surplus Apollo hardware used for the ASTP mission was not equipped with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/APAS" title="APAS">
        APAS
       </a>
       docking collar jointly developed by NASA and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Soviet Academy of Sciences">
        Soviet Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       for the mission. One end of the docking module was attached to the Apollo using the same "probe-and-
       <a href="/wiki/Drogue" title="Drogue">
        drogue
       </a>
       " docking mechanism used on the Lunar Module and the
       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">
        Skylab
       </a>
       space station, while its other end had the APAS docking collar, which Soyuz 19 carried in place of the standard Soyuz/Salyut system of the time. The APAS collar fitted onto Soyuz 19 was releasable, allowing the two spacecraft to separate in case of malfunction.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Apollo flew with a three-man crew on board:
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_P._Stafford" title="Thomas P. Stafford">
        Tom Stafford
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vance_Brand" title="Vance Brand">
        Vance Brand
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Deke_Slayton" title="Deke Slayton">
        Deke Slayton
       </a>
       . Stafford had already flown into space three times, including within eight miles of the lunar surface as Commander of Apollo 10, and was the first
       <a href="/wiki/General_officer" title="General officer">
        general officer
       </a>
       to fly into space.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slayton was one of the original
       <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Seven" title="Mercury Seven">
        Mercury Seven
       </a>
       astronauts selected in 1959, but an irregular heartbeat grounded him until 1972. He became head of NASA's astronaut office and, after a lengthy medical program, selected himself for this mission. At the time, Slayton was the oldest person to fly in space and the one with the longest gap between selection as an astronaut and first flight into space. Brand, meanwhile, had trained with the Apollo spacecraft during his time as a backup
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
        Apollo 15
       </a>
       command module pilot, and had served two stints as a backup Skylab commander. The closest he had come to flying prior to ASTP was as commander for the
       <a href="/wiki/Skylab_Rescue" title="Skylab Rescue">
        Skylab Rescue
       </a>
       mission mustered to potentially retrieve the crew of
       <a href="/wiki/Skylab_3" title="Skylab 3">
        Skylab 3
       </a>
       due to a fuel leak on that mission's Apollo CSM.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Soyuz flew with two men:
       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov" title="Alexey Leonov">
        Alexey Leonov
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Valeri_Kubasov" title="Valeri Kubasov">
        Valeri Kubasov
       </a>
       . Leonov became the first man to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">
        walk in space
       </a>
       on
       <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">
        Voskhod 2
       </a>
       in 1965. Kubasov, who flew on
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_6" title="Soyuz 6">
        Soyuz 6
       </a>
       in 1969, ran some of the earliest
       <a href="/wiki/Space_manufacturing" title="Space manufacturing">
        space manufacturing
       </a>
       experiments. Both were to have flown on the ill-fated
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_11" title="Soyuz 11">
        Soyuz 11
       </a>
       in 1971 (Leonov as commander, Kubasov as the flight engineer), but were grounded because Kubasov was suspected to have
       <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">
        tuberculosis
       </a>
       . The two-man crew on the Soyuz was a result of the modifications needed to allow the cosmonauts to wear the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sokol_pressure_suit" title="Sokol pressure suit">
        Sokol pressure suit
       </a>
       during launch, docking, and reentry.
      </p>
      <p>
       The ASTP-class
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_7K-TM" title="Soyuz 7K-TM">
        Soyuz 7K-TM
       </a>
       spacecraft used was a variation of the post-Soyuz 11 two-man design, with the batteries replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">
        solar panels
       </a>
       enabling "solo" flights (missions not docking to one of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salyut" title="Salyut">
        Salyut
       </a>
       space stations). It was designed to operate, during the docking phase, at a reduced nitrogen/oxygen pressure of 10.2 psi, allowing easier transfers between the Apollo and Soyuz. Six ASTP-class Soyuz spacecraft were built in total, including the one used. Before the actual mission, two craft were launched unmanned as Kosmos satellites. The third was launched as the manned
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_16" title="Soyuz 16">
        Soyuz 16
       </a>
       flight as a rehearsal in order to test the APAS docking mechanism. Another craft was used fully fueled as a "hot backup" at the launch site – later it was disassembled. And the sixth craft was available as a "cold" backup; it was later used on the
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_22" title="Soyuz 22">
        last "solo" Soyuz flight
       </a>
       in 1976, but with the APAS docking adapter replaced by the MKF-6 multispectral camera.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_and_mission">
        Launch and mission
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Launch and mission">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3459" data-file-width="3101" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg/220px-Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg/330px-Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg/440px-Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Imagery.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Apollo spacecraft, as seen by the Soyuz crew.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soyuz_19_(Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project)_spacecraft.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

          </a>
         </div>
         Soyuz 19 as seen from the Apollo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3117" data-file-width="4648" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg/220px-Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg/330px-Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg/440px-Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_Soyuz_Test_Project_Mission_Control.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mission control center in Houston during ASTP.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1942" data-file-width="2519" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg/220px-ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg/330px-ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg/440px-ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ASTP_handshake_-_cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The historic handshake between Stafford and Leonov
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1629" data-file-width="2475" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg/220px-President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg/330px-President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg/440px-President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Ford_talks_to_ASTP_crew.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         U.S. President
         <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">
          Gerald Ford
         </a>
         speaks to the Soviet and American crews on July 18, 1975.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg/220px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg/330px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg/440px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Commemorative_Plaque.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The astronauts and cosmonauts assembled this commemorative plaque in orbit as a symbol of the international cooperation.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Soyuz and Apollo flights launched within seven-and-a-half hours of each other on July 15, and docked on July 17. Three hours later, the two mission commanders, Stafford and Leonov, exchanged the first international handshake in space through the open hatch of the Soyuz. NASA had calculated that the historic handshake would have taken place over the British seaside resort of
       <a href="/wiki/Bognor_Regis" title="Bognor Regis">
        Bognor Regis
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but a delay resulted in its occurrence being over the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">
        Metz
       </a>
       in France.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the first crew exchange, the crews were read a statement from Soviet Premier
       <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">
        Leonid Brezhnev
       </a>
       , and received a phone call from U.S. President
       <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">
        Gerald Ford
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       While the two ships were docked, the three Americans and two Soviets conducted joint scientific experiments, exchanged flags and gifts (including tree seeds which were later planted in the two countries), signed certificates, visited each other's ships, ate together, and conversed in each other's languages. (Because of Stafford's pronounced drawl when speaking Russian, Leonov later joked that there were three languages spoken on the mission: Russian, English, and "Oklahomski.") There were also docking and redocking maneuvers, during which the two spacecraft reversed roles and the Soyuz became the "active" ship.
      </p>
      <p>
       American scientists developed four of the experiments performed during the mission. Embryologist
       <a href="/wiki/Jane_M._Oppenheimer" title="Jane M. Oppenheimer">
        Jane Oppenheimer
       </a>
       analyzed the effects of weightlessness on fish eggs at various stages of development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After 44 hours together, the two ships separated, and maneuvered to use the Apollo to create an artificial
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse" title="Solar eclipse">
        solar eclipse
       </a>
       to allow the crew of the Soyuz to take photographs of the solar
       <a href="/wiki/Corona" title="Corona">
        corona
       </a>
       . Another brief docking was made before the ships went their separate ways. The Soviets remained in space for five days, and the Americans for nine, during which the Apollo crew also conducted Earth observation experiments.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Re-entry_and_aftermath">
        Re-entry and aftermath
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Re-entry and aftermath">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The mission was considered a great success, both technically and as a public-relations exercise for both nations. The only serious problem was during reentry and
       <a href="/wiki/Splashdown" title="Splashdown">
        splashdown
       </a>
       of the Apollo craft, during which the crew were accidentally exposed to toxic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrogen_tetroxide" title="Nitrogen tetroxide">
        nitrogen tetroxide
       </a>
       fumes, caused by the
       <a href="/wiki/Reaction_control_system" title="Reaction control system">
        reaction control system
       </a>
       (RCS)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidizer" title="Oxidizer">
        oxidizer
       </a>
       venting from the spacecraft and reentering a cabin air intake. The RCS was inadvertently left on during descent, and nitrogen tetroxide was sucked into the spacecraft as it drew in outside air. Brand briefly lost consciousness, while Stafford retrieved emergency oxygen masks, put one on Brand, and gave one to Slayton. The three astronauts were hospitalized for two weeks in
       <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">
        Honolulu
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Brand took responsibility for the mishap; because of high noise levels in the cabin during reentry, he believes he was unable to hear Stafford call off one item of the reentry checklist, the closure of two switches which would have automatically shut off the RCS and initiated drogue parachute deployment. These procedures were manually performed later than usual, allowing the ingestion of the propellant fumes through the ventilation system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The ASTP was the final flight of an Apollo spacecraft. Immediately after the launch of the Apollo spacecraft, preparations began to convert
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">
        Launch Pad 39B
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">
        Vehicle Assembly Building
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">
        Kennedy Space Center
       </a>
       for use by the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttle
       </a>
       , the United States' next manned spacecraft program. Launch Pad 39A had already been closed after the launch of
       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">
        Skylab
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spacecraft_locations">
        Spacecraft locations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Spacecraft locations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Apollo Command Module from the mission is on display at the
       <a href="/wiki/California_Science_Center" title="California Science Center">
        California Science Center
       </a>
       in Los Angeles. The descent module of Soyuz 19 is on display at the
       <a href="/wiki/RKK_Energiya_museum" title="RKK Energiya museum">
        RKK Energiya museum
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Korolyov,_Moscow_Oblast" title="Korolyov, Moscow Oblast">
        Korolyov, Moscow Oblast
       </a>
       , Russia.
      </p>
      <p>
       A display at the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Air_and_Space_Museum" title="National Air and Space Museum">
        National Air and Space Museum
       </a>
       in Washington, D.C. shows the docked Apollo/Soyuz configuration with the restored Apollo Command and Service Module used for testing prior to the mission, the back-up Docking Module, and a model of the Soyuz spacecraft. An identical Soyuz model is exhibited at the
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Visitor_Complex" title="Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex">
        Kennedy Space Center Visitor Complex
       </a>
       . A full-size mockup of the two docked spacecraft is located at the
       <a href="/wiki/Cosmosphere" title="Cosmosphere">
        Cosmosphere
       </a>
       in Hutchinson, Kansas.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb noresize tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:808px;">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="">
        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-soyuz.jpg" title="The Apollo–Soyuz display in the National Air and Space Museum">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="2457" data-file-width="10214" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo-soyuz.jpg/800px-Apollo-soyuz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo-soyuz.jpg/1200px-Apollo-soyuz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Apollo-soyuz.jpg/1600px-Apollo-soyuz.jpg 2x" width="800"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Apollo-soyuz.jpg" title="File:Apollo-soyuz.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Apollo–Soyuz display in the National Air and Space Museum
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">
        Legacy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legacy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S74-24913.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3011" data-file-width="3923" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/S74-24913.jpg/220px-S74-24913.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/S74-24913.jpg/330px-S74-24913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/S74-24913.jpg/440px-S74-24913.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:S74-24913.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Apollo-Soyuz painting
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A derivative (but mechanically incompatible) docking collar,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/APAS-89" title="APAS-89">
        APAS-89
       </a>
       was launched as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kristall" title="Kristall">
        Kristall
       </a>
       module of the Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
        Mir
       </a>
       space station. Originally intended as the docking port for the (defunct)
       <a href="/wiki/Buran_(spacecraft)" title="Buran (spacecraft)">
        Buran
       </a>
       Soviet space shuttle, the APAS-89 unit was used for the next Russo-American docking mission,
       <a href="/wiki/STS-71" title="STS-71">
        STS-71
       </a>
       , twenty years later as part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Shuttle%E2%80%93Mir_Program" title="Shuttle–Mir Program">
        Shuttle–Mir Program
       </a>
       (though not before the docking port was tested by the last APAS-equipped Soyuz,
       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-16" title="Soyuz TM-16">
        TM-16
       </a>
       , in 1993).
      </p>
      <p>
       The American
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">
        Space Shuttle
       </a>
       continued to use the same APAS-89 docking hardware through the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">
        Space Shuttle program
       </a>
       to dock to Mir and then the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
        International Space Station
       </a>
       , the latter through the
       <a href="/wiki/Pressurized_Mating_Adapter" title="Pressurized Mating Adapter">
        Pressurized Mating Adapters
       </a>
       (PMAs).
      </p>
      <p>
       The PMAs are equipped with the later
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/APAS-95" title="APAS-95">
        APAS-95
       </a>
       adapters, which differ from the APAS-89 adapters in that they are no longer androgynous; while compatible with the APAS-89 docking collars, they are not capable of acting as the "active" partner in docking.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first PMA, PMA-1, remains in use as the interface connecting the Russian-built, NASA-owned
       <a href="/wiki/Zarya" title="Zarya">
        Zarya
       </a>
       module to the
       <a href="/wiki/US_Orbital_Segment" title="US Orbital Segment">
        US segment of the ISS
       </a>
       , and so the APAS continues in use to this day.
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Minor_planet" title="Minor planet">
        minor planet
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/2228_Soyuz-Apollo" title="2228 Soyuz-Apollo">
        2228 Soyuz-Apollo
       </a>
       , discovered in 1977 by Soviet astronomer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nikolai_Stepanovich_Chernykh" title="Nikolai Stepanovich Chernykh">
        Nikolai Stepanovich Chernykh
       </a>
       , is named after the mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commemorations">
        Commemorations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Commemorations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1975_CPA_4478.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2835" data-file-width="2002" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/1975_CPA_4478.jpg/170px-1975_CPA_4478.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/1975_CPA_4478.jpg/255px-1975_CPA_4478.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/1975_CPA_4478.jpg/340px-1975_CPA_4478.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1975_CPA_4478.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Soyuz–Apollon, Issue of 1975, USSR
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The US Postal Service issued the
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._space_exploration_history_on_U.S._stamps#Apollo–Soyuz_Commemorative_Issue_of_1975" title="U.S. space exploration history on U.S. stamps">
        Apollo–Soyuz commemorative stamps
       </a>
       , honoring the United States–Soviet link up in space, on July 15, 1975, the day of the launch. The remaining crew's most recent reunion was on July 16, 2010, when Leonov, Kubasov, Stafford, and Brand met at an
       <a href="/wiki/Omega_SA" title="Omega SA">
        Omega
       </a>
       timepiece store in New York City. All except Leonov participated in a public roundtable that evening. Omega had produced several watches to be used on the mission.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="575" data-file-width="1968" height="88" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg/300px-Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg/450px-Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg/600px-Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_Soyuz_1975_Issue-10c.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/U.S._space_exploration_history_on_U.S._stamps" title="U.S. space exploration history on U.S. stamps">
          Apollo–Soyuz, Issue of 1975, USA
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="center">
       <div class="thumb tnone">
        <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg">
          <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2099" data-file-width="4214" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg/250px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg/375px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg/500px-Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
         </a>
         <div class="thumbcaption">
          <div class="magnify">
           <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo-Soyuz_Test_Project_Flown_Silver_Robbins_Medallion.jpg" title="Enlarge">
           </a>
          </div>
          Apollo-Soyuz Test Project Medallion
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Monument">
        Monument
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Monument">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the wake of the mission, a large Apollo–Soyuz monument was constructed outside
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TsUP" title="TsUP">
        TsUP
       </a>
       (the Soviet, later Russian space control center) in Moscow. It consisted of a metal Earth overarched by an arc terminating in a scale model of the joined Apollo–Soyuz spacecraft. It was damaged when a vehicle collided with it in the late 1990s
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       , and was removed for repairs.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Program_cost">
        Program cost
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Program cost">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w.svg">
           <img alt="Wiki letter w.svg" data-file-height="44" data-file-width="44" height="44" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/44px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/66px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6c/Wiki_letter_w.svg/88px-Wiki_letter_w.svg.png 2x" width="44"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           is missing information about how much the Soviet Union spent on Soyuz 19
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please expand the section to include this information. Further details may exist on the
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Apollo%E2%80%93Soyuz_Test_Project" title="Talk:Apollo–Soyuz Test Project">
            talk page
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (April 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The United States spent $245 million on Apollo–Soyuz, or $1 billion in 2010 inflation-adjusted dollars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lafleur20100308_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-lafleur20100308-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <ul>
       <li>
        In the non-canonical
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Superman_(comic_book)" title="Superman (comic book)">
          Superman
         </a>
        </i>
        #300 and
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Superman:_Red_Son" title="Superman: Red Son">
          Superman: Red Son
         </a>
        </i>
        comic books, the Apollo–Soyuz astronauts and cosmonauts see an
        <a href="/wiki/Unidentified_flying_object" title="Unidentified flying object">
         unidentified flying object
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Clark_Kent" title="Clark Kent">
         Kal-El
        </a>
        's spacecraft) approaching Earth, then the USA and the USSR race to the capsule to take it in their nation.
       </li>
       <li>
        The 2009 film
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Night_at_the_Museum:_Battle_of_the_Smithsonian" title="Night at the Museum: Battle of the Smithsonian">
          Night at the Museum: Battle of the Smithsonian
         </a>
        </i>
        features the Apollo–Soyuz display conserved at the National Air &amp; Space Museum.
       </li>
       <li>
        In 2013, the Apollo–Soyuz Test Project was discussed in
        <a href="/wiki/Pilot_(The_Americans)" title="Pilot (The Americans)">
         the pilot episode
        </a>
        of the FX show
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Americans_(2013_TV_series)" title="The Americans (2013 TV series)">
          The Americans
         </a>
        </i>
        , with Stafford being portrayed by an extra.
       </li>
       <li>
        The 2017 film
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Valerian_and_the_City_of_a_Thousand_Planets" title="Valerian and the City of a Thousand Planets">
          Valerian and the City of a Thousand Planets
         </a>
        </i>
        features the Apollo–Soyuz Test Project in its opening credits.
       </li>

        <li id="cite_note-1">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-1">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation book">
           <a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Samuels" title="Richard J. Samuels">
            Samuels, Richard J.
           </a>
           , ed. (December 21, 2005).
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=K751AwAAQBAJ&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;pg=PT747#v=onepage&amp;q=Apollo-Soyuz&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">
            <i>
             Encyclopedia of United States National Security
            </i>
           </a>
           (1st ed.).
           <a href="/wiki/SAGE_Publications" title="SAGE Publications">
            SAGE Publications
           </a>
           . p. 669.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-7619-2927-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-7619-2927-7">
            978-0-7619-2927-7
           </a>
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             May 25,
            </span>
            2016
           </span>
           .
           <q>
            Most observers felt that the U.S. moon landing ended the space race with a decisive American victory. […] The formal end of the space race occurred with the 1975 joint Apollo-Soyuz mission, in which U.S. and Soviet spacecraft docked, or joined, in orbit while their crews visited one another's craft and performed joint scientific experiments.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedia+of+United+States+National+Security&amp;rft.pages=669&amp;rft.edition=1st&amp;rft.pub=SAGE+Publications&amp;rft.date=2005-12-21&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-7619-2927-7&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DK751AwAAQBAJ%26lpg%3DPP1%26pg%3DPT747%23v%3Donepage%26q%3DApollo-Soyuz%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AApollo%E2%80%93Soyuz+Test+Project">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Space+Review&amp;rft.atitle=Costs+of+US+piloted+programs&amp;rft.date=2010-03-08&amp;rft.au=Lafleur%2C+Claude&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.thespacereview.com%2Farticle%2F1579%2F1&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AApollo%E2%80%93Soyuz+Test+Project">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
       </ol>
